PREFACE

** рдЖрд╕реЗрдЪрдирдХрд░рд╛рдорд╛рдпрдгрдореН** otherwise known as рд░рд╛рдорд╛рдпрдгрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛ is a short and sweet poem in Arya metrer. The peculiar feature of this work is that the first three p─Бdas of each ┼Ыloka narrate the story and the fourth p─Бda embodies the moral suggested by the incidents contained therein. The poem opens with the N─Бrada’s interview with V─Бlm─лki and not a single event has been omitted in the story.

The author of this work, the late Brahmasri Subrahmanya Suri, my revered father, was born in 1850 at Kadayakkudi, a village about 5 miles to the South of Pudukkotta. He was a Samavedi Brahmin of Kausika Gotra and a descendant of Cokkanatha Dikshita (fatherтАУinтАУlaw of Ramabhadra Dikshita, author of JanakiтАУparinayam) a distinguished Grammarian early in the
Seventeenth Century.

The ancestors of the family are stated to have been in Nachikurichi a village now in a decayed state, adjoining Bommasamudram, Trichinopoly Taluq and thence migrated to Pinnangudy, a village in the state of Pudukkotta. The author’s father Brahmasri Sankaranarayana Sastrial settled at Kadayakkudi where he married Srimati Subbalakshmi the only daughter of Brahmasri Ramaswami Sastrial.

The author received his education in рдХрд╛рд╡реНрдп, рдирд╛рдЯрдХ andрдЕрд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░under Brahmasri Swami Iyengar of Kadayakkudi

and inрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдХрд░рдгunder Brahmasri Srinivasa Seshacharya of Karavayal a village in Arantangi Taluq, Tanjore District. He secured a high degree of proficiency in Sanskrit Literature, Rhetoric and Grammar. In addition to his eminence as a Sanskrit Scholar, he was a fine musician and a finer poet and he had also an exquisite taste for drawing. As he was extremely pious and devoted, his skill in drawing was directed towards drawing pictures of various deities in different postures which were being hung in his p┼лj─Бgrha. He was also well known for his Harikath─Б performances especially for his fine voice, erudite exposition and sincere devotion. For this purpose, he composed many charitrams in Sanskrit adapted to music though I regret to state that very few of the manuscripts are now with me. He was held in high esteem by the late Sir A. Seshia Sastrial, Dewan of Pudukkotta. He entered the Raja’s College Pudukkotta as assistant Sanskrit pandit on 19-1-1884 and retired as Head Sanskrit pandit on 16-2-1910.

His other works are. (1) рд╡рд▓реНрд▓реАрдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓реЗрдпрдореН a Sanskrit drama in seven acts recently published by me. (2) **рдЪрддреБрд╖реНрдкрджреАрдЪрддрд┐рд╢реНрд╢рддреАтАФ**a literal translation in verse of<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1699352080Screenshot2023-11-07154429.png"/> (3) рдордиреНрдордердорд╛рджрдирдореН a Bhana in one act published in a Journal some 30 years back. (4) Miscellaneous works such as (a) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзреБрдирд┐рдХрд╡реГрддреНрддрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рд┐рдХрд╛, (b) рд╡реГрддреНрддрдирд╛рдорд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ, (c) рдХрд╛рд░рдХрд╛рдгрд┐ and рд▓рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдГ in verses, (d) charitrams adapted to music viz.,рд░рд╛рдорд╛рд╡рддрд╛рд░,рд╕реАрддрд╛рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдореН, рд░реБрдХреНрдорд┐рдгреАрдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдореН, рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╡рддреАрдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдореН, рдорд╛рд░рд╕реЛрдордпрд╛рдЬрд┐рдЪрд░рд┐рддреНрд░рдореН, рд╡рд┐рднреВрддрд┐рдорд╛рд╣рд╛рддреНрдореНрдпрдореН etc. (e) рд╣рд▓реНрд▓реАрд╕рд╕реНрддреБрддрдпрдГ such as рд░рд╛рдордЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдкрджреНрдпрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд░рддреНрдирдореН рд╢реБрдХрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд┐-

рд╕реБрдзрд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдпрдирдореН, рдмреГрд╣рджрдВрдмрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдХрд╣рд▓реНрд▓реАрд╕рд╛рдГ <MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1699358729Screenshot2023-11-07173511.png"/>, рд╣рд░рддреАрд░реНрдереЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рджрд╢рдХрдореН, рд░рд╛рдорд╛рдпрдгрд╣рд▓реНрд▓реАрд╕рд╛рдГ, рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╡рддреАрдкрд░рд┐рдгрдпрд╣рд▓реНрд▓рд╛рдВрд╕рд╛рдГ рдбреЛрд▓рд╛рдЧреАрддрд╛рдирд┐ and others.

[(e) in now in press.]

An important workрдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рд╕рдиреНрджреЗрд╢ and several other рдХреГрддрд┐тАЩs in praise of рдХрдкрд╛рд▓реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ and рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕рд╛рд░рдерд┐ composed by the author during his stay with me just before his demise in October, 1913, were unfortnately lost while travelling in train.

To avoid further loss of the very few works with me, the filial duty to the departed soul prompted me to publish the same as far as I can and I will be highly thankful if the lovers of Sanskrit Literature are kind enough to enlighten me on the errors which might have been committed by me while seeing the work through the press.

Mylapore,
1-1-1932.

S. SANKARANARAYANAN,
Superintendent,
Accountant General’s Office,
Madras.
